                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-right" style="max-width:500px;">
                     <div class="text-body-wrapper W-100 Font-B-1-160">
                      <noscript>
                      </noscript>
                      <div class="text-body W-100 Font-B-1-160" id="article-aft-text-body-105364187302" style="color:#222222;max-width:500px;">
                       <div class="body read-more-cut">
                        <div class="pre-cut" style="height:auto;margin-bottom:1.5em;">
                         <p>
                          <img alt="The Best Part of Having An Average Face" height="623" src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/8f3aa31506fc8a60cc97a611eb9cb3646f781cd7.jpg" width="500"/>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <em>
                           <strong>
                            The average face of female residents of Sydney, Australia, depicted by the artist Mike Mike.
                           </strong>
                           (Image created by Mike Mike |
                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:2b477108-734a-34f7-83f0-d5830f4c1121;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://faceoftomorrow.org/" target="_blank">
                            Faceoftomorrow.org
                           </a>
                           )
                          </em>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          While its human nature to marvel at a beautiful face, science says we may not exactly view the characteristics of pretty people in the most glowing light.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          According to
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:2b477108-734a-34f7-83f0-d5830f4c1121;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://pss.sagepub.com/content/early/2014/12/11/0956797614554955.abstract" target="_blank">
                           new research
                          </a>
                          published in the journal
                          <em>
                           Psychological Science
                          </em>
                          , having a typical face has its benefits, as people seem to consider the faces of Average Joes and Plain Janes the most trustworthy.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          To conduct the study, researchers digitally combined the faces of 92 different women to get a sum of parts: a typical face. They also conjured up an attractive face by averaging the faces of the 12 most attractive women in another set of photos.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/042c099c12f9aca78fd7acc64c69f58a372cf767.jpg" height="132" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="500"/>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <em>
                           <strong>
                            The typical face was found to be more trustworthy than those on the opposite sides of the spectrum.
                           </strong>
                           (Carmel Sofer|Psychological Science)
                          </em>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          After creating these digital images, they joined the typical face and attractive face into one, and then created nine more images varying in levels of attractiveness and typicality. The final outcome? A total of 11 faces, which were laid out along a spectrum from least attractive to most attractive, with the typical face smack dab in the middle.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          To nix gender bias, the researchers had only women rate the faces on a 9-point scale for trustworthiness or attractiveness. Over the course of the study, they wound up rating each separate face a total of three times.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/2412a75d6db7f4b6324ed93b6290d40f3e57b45c.jpg" height="534" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="500"/>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <em>
                           <strong>
                            The average face lies at the intersection of trustworthiness and attractiveness.
                           </strong>
                           (Carmel Sofer|Psychological Science)
                          </em>
                         </p>
                        </div>
                        <div class="post-cut W-100" id="post-cut" style="transition-property:none;-webkit-transition-property:none;transition-duration:10s;-webkit-transition-duration:10s;transition-timing-function:ease-in;-webkit-transition-timing-function:ease-in;overflow:hidden;max-height:0;max-width:500px;">
                         <p>
                          The scientists found that the results revealed something of a U-shape correlation between trustworthiness and attractiveness; the closer an image was to the typical face in the middle of the spectrum, the more trustworthy the women rated it. Attractiveness, on the other hand, had nothing to do with typicality. As expected, moving beyond the central image and up the spectrum, the participants rated each face as more and more attractive.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          So, why would we trust someone with a typical face? Its simple: generally, were comfortable with what we know and recognize, while we fear the unknown.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Face typicality likely indicates familiarity and cultural affiliation  as such, these findings have important implications for understanding social perception, including cross-cultural perceptions and interactions, says lead researcher Carmel Sofer, a psychological scientist at Princeton University and Radboud University Nijmegen in the Netherlands, in a
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:2b477108-734a-34f7-83f0-d5830f4c1121;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.psychologicalscience.org/index.php/news/releases/people-trust-typical-looking-faces-most.html" target="_blank">
                           press release
                          </a>
                          .
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          With all the science on the potential benefits of being beautiful 
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:2b477108-734a-34f7-83f0-d5830f4c1121;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://press.princeton.edu/titles/9516.html" target="_blank">
                           higher pay
                          </a>
                          ,
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:2b477108-734a-34f7-83f0-d5830f4c1121;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://psych.colorado.edu/~tito/sp03/7536/Rhodes_et_al_2001.pdf" target="_blank">
                           better health
                          </a>
                          , the list goes on  at least we know beautiful people dont have it
                          <em>
                           all
                          </em>
                          .
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           Your Next Read:
                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:2b477108-734a-34f7-83f0-d5830f4c1121;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.yahoo.com/health/5-brain-tricks-to-improve-your-workout-104950869902.html" target="_blank">
                            <em>
                             5 Brain Tricks to Improve Your Workout
                            </em>
                           </a>
                          </strong>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                         </p>
                        </div>

                         Ftiness
                        </a>
                       </div>
                       <a data-action-outcome="open" data-routable-url="/health/1/treadmill-injuries-one-womans-story-underscores-124001279742.html" data-ylk="g:46862e17-5d42-3825-ab2b-11ba5e6fa426;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:also;ad:0;cpos:3;itc:0;t8:tileview;t9:21;elm:img;elmt:ct;" href="/health/treadmill-injuries-one-womans-story-underscores-124001279742.html" style="color:#000;">
                        <span class="item-title Font-A-3-120 D-b" style="word-wrap:break-word;margin-left:175px;">
                         Treadmill Injuries: One Womans StoryUnderscores Importance of Simple Safety Tips

40\u002F097fd60b9b6c862215909a9c50c0a5260010c767.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":540,"height":434,"size_type":"original","formats":{}}],"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002Foriginal\u002FDnJrMY4-snLcV5q61ywNJ0j6_U8","source_url":"http:\u002F\u002F41.media.tumblr.com\u002F8b53ddf61b7062b1e2947b19ce24351f\u002Ftumblr_inline_nrg5r42xop1t4rmqt_540.jpg"}],"highlight_color":"#000000","data_version":"1","title":"Pentagon Announces Plan Aimed at Lifting Transgender Ban in Military","summary":"Defense Secretary Ash Carter says the Pentagons current regulations banning transgender individuals from serving in the military are outdated, and anyone willing to serve the country should be able to do so.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F097fd60b9b6c862215909a9c50c0a5260010c767.jpg\" width=\"540\" height=\"434\" alt=\"Pentagon Announces Plan Aimed at Lifting Transgender Ban in Military\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EOver the next six months, a working group in at the Pentagon will be studying the impact of lifting the military&#x2019;s transgender ban.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E (Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDefense Secretary Ash Carter says the Pentagon&#x2019;s current regulations banning transgender individuals from serving in the military are outdated, and anyone willing to serve the country should be able to do so.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ECarter is creating a working group to do a six-month study on the impact of lifting the ban. Carter says the group will begin with the presumption that transgender people should be able to serve openly.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe plan, which was first reported by The Associated Press, gives the services time to work through questions about health care, housing, physical standards, uniforms and costs associated with the change.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDuring that time, transgender individuals would still be unable to join the military, but decisions to force out those already serving would be referred to the Pentagon&#x2019;s acting undersecretary for personnel.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWith the six-month study, military chiefs wanted time to methodically work through the legal, medical and administrative issues and develop training to ease any transition, and senior leaders believed six months would be sufficient.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe officials said Defense Secretary Ash Carter has asked his personnel undersecretary, Brad Carson, to set up a working group of senior military and civilian leaders to take an objective look at the issue. One senior official said that while the goal is to lift the ban, Carter wants the working group to look at the practical effects, including the costs, and determine whether it would affect readiness or create any insurmountable problems that could derail the plan. The group would also develop uniform guidelines.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fsenior-airman-logan-ireland-is-one-of-over-15-000-120775992272.html\"\u003ETransgender Troops - At War, In Love, and Fighting to Serve Openly\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDuring the six months, transgender individuals would still not be able to join the military, but any decisions to force out those already serving would be referred to the Pentagon&#x2019;s acting undersecretary for personnel, the officials said. One senior official said the goal was to avoid forcing any transgender service members to leave during that time.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESeveral officials familiar with the planning spoke on condition of anonymity because they were not authorized to talk about the issue publicly before the final details have been worked out.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn a statement to The Associated Press, Carter said, &#x201C;we must ensure that everyone who&#x2019;s able and willing to serve has the full and equal opportunity to do so. And we must treat all of our people with the dignity and respect they deserve. Going forward the Department of Defense must and will continue to improve how we do both.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESome of the key concerns involved in the repeal of the ban include whether the military would conduct or pay for the medical costs, surgeries and other treatment associated with any gender transition, as well as which physical training or testing standards transgender individuals would be required to meet during different stages of their transition.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOfficials said the military also wants time to tackle questions about where transgender troops would be housed, what uniforms they would wear, what berthing they would have on ships, which bathrooms they would use and whether their presence would affect the ability of small units to work well together. The military has dealt with many similar questions as it integrated the ranks by race, gender and sexual orientation.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETransgender people &#x2014; those who identify with a different gender than they were born with and sometimes take hormone treatments or have surgery to develop the physical characteristics of their preferred gender &#x2014; are banned from military service. But studies and other surveys have estimated that as many as 15,000 transgender people serve in the active duty military and the reserves, often in secret but in many cases with the knowledge of their unit commander or peers.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Obviously this isn&#x2019;t finished, but Secretary Carter&#x2019;s clear statement of intent means that transgender service members should and will be treated with the same dignity as other service members,&#x201D; said Allyson Robinson, Army veteran and policy director for an association of lesbian, gay, bisexual and transgender military personnel called Service members, Partners, and Allies for Respect and Tolerance for All, or SPARTA.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe move follows several weeks of high level meetings in the Pentagon among top ranking military chiefs, secretaries and Defense Department leaders, including one on Monday involving Carter and the chiefs of the various services.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EMilitary leaders have pointed to the gradual - and ultimately successful - transition after the ban on gays serving openly in the military was lifted in 2011. Although legislation repealing that ban passed Congress in late 2010, the military services spent months conducting training and reviews before the decision actually took effect the following September.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fsee-a-transgender-mans-joy-as-he-hones-his-new-121760390117.html\"\u003ESee a Transgender Man&#x2019;s Joy as He Hones His New Body &#x2014; and Meet the Gym That Got Him There&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe latest Pentagon move comes just weeks after the Supreme Court upheld the right of same-sex couples to marry.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOfficials familiar with the Pentagon meetings said the chiefs of the Army, Navy, Marine Corps and Air Force did not express opposition to lifting the ban. Instead, they said the military leaders asked for time to figure out health care, housing and other questions and also to provide information and training to the troops to insure a smooth transition.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAlthough guidelines require that transgender individuals be dismissed from the military, the services in recent months have required more senior leaders to make the final decisions on those cases, effectively slowing the dismissal process.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe transgender issue came to the fore as the military struggled with how to deal with convicted national security leaker Chelsea Manning&#x2019;s request for hormone therapy and other treatment while she&#x2019;s in prison. Manning, arrested as Bradley Manning, is the first transgender military prisoner to request such treatment, and the Army approved the hormone therapy, under pressure from a lawsuit.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EManning, is serving a 35-year sentence. The former intelligence analyst was convicted in August 2013 of espionage and other offenses for sending more than 700,000 classified documents to WikiLeaks while working in with Severe Allergies Susceptible to Rebound Reactions, Study Finds","summary":"These delayed reactions tend to occur when the initial symptoms of an allergic reaction go away, but then return hours or even days later  without additional exposure to the substance that caused the allergic reaction.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fba024d5cd9f04549fb8321a2172aea4664756a8e.jpg\" width=\"540\" height=\"367\" alt=\"Kids with Severe Allergies Susceptible to &#x2018;Rebound&#x2019; Reactions, Study Finds\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThese delayed reactions tend to occur when the initial symptoms of an allergic reaction go away, but then return hours or even days later &#x2014; without additional exposure to the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.livescience.com\u002F36041-common-food-allergies.html\"\u003Esubstance that caused the allergic reaction.\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E(Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIt&#x2019;s fairly common for children who have a severe allergic reaction known as anaphylaxis to be in danger of having a second, delayed allergic reaction within hours of the first one, a new study suggests.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EResearchers in Canada found that about 15 percent of children who came to the emergency room for anaphylaxis had a second \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.livescience.com\u002F48636-this-girl-nearly-died-from-orange-allergy.html\"\u003Eserious allergic reaction hours\u003C\u002Fa\u003E after the initial reaction.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe study also found that about 75 percent of these second anaphylactic reactions, known as biphasic reactions, occurred within 6 hours of their first anaphylaxis symptoms, and in most cases, the children were still at the ER because of their first reaction. The children&#x2019;s symptoms included difficulty breathing, low blood pressure, hives or swelling, nausea and dizziness.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;The study found that delayed reactions were more likely to happen if the initial allergic reaction in children was severe, and if it was not treated with epinephrine,&#x201D; said Dr. Waleed Alqurashi, the study&#x2019;s lead author and an emergency physician at Children&#x2019;s Hospital of Eastern Ontario in Ottawa, Canada.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.livescience.com\u002F35479-nine-weirdest-allergies-110215.html\"\u003E8\u003Ci\u003E Strange Signs You&#x2019;re Having an Allergic Reaction\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThese delayed reactions tend to occur when the initial symptoms of an allergic reaction go away, but then return hours or even days later &#x2014; without additional exposure to the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.livescience.com\u002F36041-common-food-allergies.html\"\u003Esubstance that caused the allergic reaction\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, he said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EOne possible reason children may develop these delayed allergic reactions is that they seem to experience an inflammatory response that lasts longer than it does in adults, Alqurashi said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn children, common triggers of these serious allergic reactions might include insect stings, medications, and foods like nuts, seafood, milk and eggs, he said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAn anaphylactic reaction is a medical emergency requiring immediate treatment with a shot of the hormone epinephrine (adrenaline). Many kids who are at risk of having these serious allergic reactions are advised to carry \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.livescience.com\u002F42321-know-how-to-use-epipen.html\"\u003Ean EpiPen\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, a prescription medication that can be self-administered or given by a parent or school nurse, to control symptoms that can come on rapidly and worsen quickly and, in some cases, be fatal. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EDelayed treatment\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe occurrence of anaphylactic reactions in children seems to be on the rise, according to the researchers. But there&#x2019;s limited information about how frequently children go on to have a second severe allergic reaction, or about which children might be more vulnerable to having them.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn the study, published online June 22 in the journal Annals of Allergy, Asthma and Immunology, the researchers analyzed the medical records of about 500 children who were treated at the emergency rooms of two large Canadian children&#x2019;s hospitals over a one-year period.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe findings suggested that children who may be at increased risk for delayed allergic reactions are those who were given medications for asthma at the hospital, had signs of anaphylactic shock when they arrived at the emergency room and needed multiple treatments with epinephrine for their initial anaphylactic reaction, Alqurashi said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn addition, the results showed that anaphylaxis tended to be more severe in children when epinephrine administration was delayed.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Epinephrine is the single \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.livescience.com\u002F41181-obama-signs-epipen-law.html\"\u003Emost important treatment for anaphylaxis\u003C\u002Fa\u003E,&#x201D; Alqurashi said. He explained that, when the drug is given promptly after the start of an allergic reaction, it controls and limits the immune system&#x2019;s response to a known allergy trigger. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;The key message for parents, caregivers and first responders is to administer epinephrine at the first sign of a severe allergic reaction to prevent anaphylaxis from worsening,&#x201D; Alqurashi said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAfter that, people should get to the emergency room, he said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMore from LiveScience:&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.livescience.com\u002F35479-nine-weirdest-allergies-110215.html\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003E9 Weirdest Allergies\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.livescience.com\u002F36041-common-food-allergies.html\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003EWhat Are the Most Common Food Allergies?\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca Injuries: One Womans StoryUnderscores Importance of Simple Safety Tips","summary":"As was her regular routine, 57-year-old sales exec Yvonne Myers stepped on the treadmill at her local gym for a run. That's when disaster struck. My nose and face were cut to pieces and my arms were throbbing from burns.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F7bb416f3afaefea452e070c44263cef1985b0d6b.jpg\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" alt=\"Treadmill Injuries: One Woman&#x2019;s Story&#xA0;Underscores Importance of Simple Safety Tips\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003E&#x201C;My nose and face were cut to pieces and my arms were throbbing from burns.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E&#xA0;\u003Ci\u003E(Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAs was her regular routine, 57-year-old sales exec Yvonne Myers stepped on the treadmill at her local gym for a run. She did not expect, however, for the machine to throw her to the ground the moment she stepped on.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe treadmill&#x2019;s previous user had not turned the machine off, and the belt was spinning at such a fast clip that it looked motionless. When Myers hit the surface, she tried to get up, but was tossed from the exercise machine instead.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;My nose and face were cut to pieces and my arms were throbbing from burns,&#x201D; the South Manchester, UK mother-of-four told \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.dailymail.co.uk\u002Ffemail\u002Farticle-3158486\u002FMaimed-TREADMILL-Mother-four-s-horror-one-thousands-badly-injured-running-machine.html\"\u003EThe Daily Mail\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. &#x201C;I also had a gash on my forehead. I looked as though I&#x2019;d been in a fight.&quot;Even regular gym-goers like Myers, who was an avid treadmill user, are not immune to the dangers of this piece of exercise equipment.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThis also isn&#x2019;t the first time treadmill accidents have made news in recent months.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESurveyMonkey CEO Dave Goldberg, husband of Facebook COO Sheryl Sandberg, died this year in a tragic treadmill accident. On May 1, he fell off a machine while on vacation in Mexico, potentially \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.people.com\u002Farticle\u002Fsheryl-sandberg-husband-died-heart-related-causes-dave-goldberg\"\u003Edue to heart complications\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and sustained a head injury, according to a report in \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.nytimes.com\u002F2015\u002F05\u002F05\u002Ftechnology\u002Fdave-goldberg-cause-of-death.html?smid=nytnow-share&amp;smprod=nytnow&amp;_r=0\"\u003EThe New York Times\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWe don&#x2019;t often think of danger when we head to the gym, but stepping on a treadmill always poses risks. In 2014, around 24,400 injuries occurred as the direct result of treadmill use &#x2014; almost 40 percent of the 62,600 injuries from exercise equipment, making these machines the most dangerous you&#x2019;ll find in your gym.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EDeaths\u003C\u002Fi\u003E from treadmill use, on the other hand, are much rarer, according to U.S. Consumer Product Safety Commission data. Only 30 fatalities from treadmills were reported between 2003 and 2012, for an average of just three per yearHere are some checks to make before you start exercising, or while you&#x2019;re in the middle of a workout, from Michael Jonesco, MD, a sports medicine physician at The Ohio State University Wexner Medical Center:&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EEnter with a clean bill of health.\u003C\u002Fb\u003EYour top priority before you hit the gym is to make sure you know your health status. &#x201C;A lot of times we&#x2019;ll see, if you&#x2019;re running, why did he collapse?&#x201D;Jonesco tells Yahoo Health. &#x201C;The most common cause of falling is a vascular event, like a heart attack. I don&#x2019;t know this case, but before you start a workout, always make sure you have a clean bill of health. Continue to be screened for coronary issues, even if you feel healthy &#x2013; especially if you have risk factors like age, being male, or a high-stress job.&#x201D;&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EBeware of strange symptoms.\u003C\u002Fb\u003EIf you&#x2019;re on the treadmill and you feel any chest pain, any shortness of breath beyond what you&#x2019;re used to in a given workout, or any lightheadedness, you need to step off. &#x201C;Lightheadedness is one most people don&#x2019;t think of,&#x201D;says Jonesco. &#x201C;But it can show you&#x2019;re not getting enough blood supply to the brain, and be a preceding factor for passing out.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EDon\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E&#x2019;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cb\u003Et add distractions (until you\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E&#x2019;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cb\u003Ere comfortable).\u003C\u002Fb\u003EBesides coronary issues, other reasons for treadmill falls can usually be pinned to distraction. &#x201C;Usually you have a comfort zone if you&#x2019;re on a machine you&#x2019;re used to, but if you&#x2019;re on vacation or using an unfamiliar machine, you want to take time to get used to it,&#x201D;Jonesco says. Start your workout at a slower pace, be aware of the width of the band, and ditch the headphones or TV until you find your rhythm.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002F7-treadmill-mistakes-you-might-be-making-91318038937.html?soc_src=mail&amp;soc_trk=ma\"\u003ETreadmill Mistakes You May Be Making\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EUse the safety tabs. \u003C\u002Fb\u003EYou know the attachments on the treadmill, that are meant to immediately stop the machine if you step out of line? They might be annoying, but use &#x2018;em, says Jonesco. &#x201C;A lot of people overlook the safety tabs because they&#x2019;re clunky, but they&#x2019;re there for a reason.&#x201D;Those attachments could prevent a fall, and are especially important if your treadmill is close to the wall in an unfamiliar area. &#x201C;I like to move the machine away from the wall if at all possible,&#x201D;Jonesco says. &#x201C;If you fall and it doesn&#x2019;t turn off, you can get pushed up against the wall, the band will keep moving and can give you some pretty bad abrasions.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EKeep help nearby.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003EAccording to the report, Goldberg wasn&#x2019;t found by his brother until 7 p.m., although he left for the gym at 4 p.m. Although the gym seems pretty safe, still tell someone you&#x2019;re going &#x2014; or preferably, take them along. &#x201C;Have a workout buddy, or at least familiarize yourself with the people around you at the gym or the staff if something were to happen,&#x201D;says Jonesco. &#x201C;Keep your cell phone nearby you in case of an emergency.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002F7-ways-to-make-your-treadmill-runs-more-effective-107228499668.html?soc_src=mail&amp;soc_trk=ma\"\u003E7 Ways To Make Your Treadmill Run More Effective&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ENevertheless, exercise is essential. Just, like anything, don&#x2019;t take safety as a given. Always be smart about using equipment, says Jonesco. &#x201C;It&#x2019;s very sad, and could have been a freak thing,&#x201D;he explains. &#x201C;The benefits of exercise far, far exceed the risks.&#x201D;\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ELet&#x2019;s keep in touch! \n\u003Cp\u003EA \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.reuters.com\u002Farticle\u002F2015\u002F06\u002F17\u002Favvo-inc-survey-idUSnPnc2dhXv+82+PRN20150617\"\u003Enew survey\u003C\u002Fa\u003E of more than 2,000 people conducted by the online legal services marketplace Avvo suggests that people who live on the west coast are more likely to be cheaters.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAccording to survey results, 20 percent of west coasters say they&#x2019;ve cheated on a partner, compared to 17 percent of southerners, 16 percent of people in the northeast, and 10 percent of Midwesterners.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.womenshealthmag.com\u002Fsex-and-relationships\u002Fsigns-hes-cheating?cid=Synd_Yahoo_July15_6SignsHesProbablyCheatingonYou\"\u003E6 Signs He&#x2019;s Probably Cheating on You\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EMen were also more likely to cop to getting some on the side, with 20 percent of those surveyed saying they&#x2019;ve had sex with someone who wasn&#x2019;t their partner. (On the flipside, 13 percent of women said they&#x2019;ve cheated.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBut let&#x2019;s go back to the west coast&#x2026;what&#x2019;s that about? Licensed clinical psychologist Ramani Durvasula, Ph.D., says it may be more about where on the west coast most of the survey respondents lived. If people in larger cities participated, then she&#x2019;s not shocked by the findings.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;These cities are filled with transplants,&#x201D; she says. &#x201C;The very personality traits that lead to someone relocating are likely to result in greater openness, and that can also translate into more &#x2018;a-moral&#x2019; behaviors, such as cheating.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.womenshealthmag.com\u002Fsex-and-relationships\u002Fhaving-an-affair?cid=Synd_Yahoo_July15_ShouldYouALWAYSTellYourPartnerifYouCheat\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003EShould You ALWAYS Tell Your Partner if You Cheat?\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EShe points out that L.A. in particular might have a higher-than-normal rate of cheaters since it&#x2019;s a creative city that &#x201C;may be more populated by those higher in the trait of openness, which may be more likely to translate into infidelity.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EOf course, psychiatrist Gail Saltz, M.D., author of \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.amazon.com\u002FAnatomy-Secret-Life-Psychology-Living\u002Fdp\u002F0767922743\"\u003EAnatomy of a Secret Life: The Psychology of Living a Lie\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, points out that infidelity happens everywhere, and people who live on the west coast shouldn&#x2019;t suddenly freak out and assume that their partner will cheat. (And the reverse is true, too&#x2014;Midwesterners shouldn&#x2019;t be super smug about their apparently lack of cheating.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EShe says other factors are much more likely to increase the risk that a person will cheat, like whether they&#x2019;ve been raised with infidelity in their family, if they&#x2019;re in a much more liberal environment where a lot of people aren&#x2019;t getting married, and if there is a lot of cheating happening around them. &#x201C;That will change your perception of how okay it is to be unfaithful,&#x201D; she says.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca Once, Will They Cheat Again?\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EOf course, no cheating is good, and it sucks that anyone reports doing it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBut there is a positive side to the study: Nearly 95 percent of the people surveyed say they&#x2019;re happy in their relationship.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E {"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F711e45012eb3aba60d4f9bbc1c1665fbdbfcbaca.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":500,"height":332,"size_type":"500","formats":{}},{"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F711e45012eb3aba60d4f9bbc1c1665fbdbfcbaca.jpg","type":"image\u002Fjpeg","width":540,"height":359,"size_type":"original","formats":{}}],"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002Foriginal\u002FZpoxXPqvpCwft3Q2YWzcbfaBjSo","source_url":"http:\u002F\u002F36.media.tumblr.com\u002Ff96f21dfbb9cbd5434b5f4065a9dc1dd\u002Ftumblr_inline_nr8cvaG66X1t58yg4_540.jpg"}],"highlight_color":"#000000","data_version":"1","title":"One Womans Story Highlights theHidden Skin Cancer Risks for People of Color","summary":"When Jacqueline Smith discovered an almond-sized lump on her bikini line, the concerned college senior went to her campus health center to find out what it could be. She was told it was an inflamed hair follicle, but that was wrong.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fb4f536060e46b7a8df3ba09dab1e2d070fb8e3be.jpg\" alt=\"One Woman&#x2019;s Story Highlights the&#xA0;Hidden Skin Cancer Risks for People of Color\" width=\"540\" height=\"394\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EWhile Caucasians are more likely to be diagnosed with skin cancer, only 16 percent of cases involve advanced-stage cancer. In comparison, 52 percent of African-Americans and 26 percent of Hispanic patients are diagnosed with late-stage cases.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E (Photo: Getty Images\u002FBrand X Pictures)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhen Jacqueline Smith discovered an almond-sized lump on her bikini line, the concerned college senior went to her campus health center to find out what it could be. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThere, she was told not to worry &#x2014; it was simply an inflamed hair follicle. But Jacqueline couldn&#x2019;t shake the feeling that the firm, unmoving lump was something more serious. After graduation, she headed back home to Hackensack, N.J., and saw her family&#x2019;s primary care physician for a second opinion. He referred her to a surgical oncologist, who biopsied the site and had dire news: Jacqueline had skin cancer, a stage IIIC melanoma that had metastasized and was just a whisper shy of slipping into stage IV cancer. &#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EA shocking diagnosis for anyone to handle, Jacqueline was especially incredulous: She was a young African-American woman with no family history of skin cancer, and she had never engaged in behaviors like tanning that studies show correlate with a higher risk.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I was totally shocked by the diagnosis &#x2014; my first thought was, &#x2018;Melanoma is the \u003Ci\u003Edeadly\u003C\u002Fi\u003E skin cancer&#x2019; &#x2014; I never had a reason for it to be on my radar, and never thought I had to prevent it,&#x201D; Jacqueline tells Yahoo Health. &#x201C;I had always heard melanoma was a risk for fair-skinned, middle-aged Caucasian women.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"359\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F711e45012eb3aba60d4f9bbc1c1665fbdbfcbaca.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EJacqueline Smith has survived two melanoma diagnoses. \u003C\u002Fb\u003E(Photo: Courtesy of Jacqueline Smith)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EJacqueline, who&#x2019;s now working as the regional assistant for New York Sen. Kirsten Gillibrand, had the cancerous lymph nodes removed when she was just 21 years old. Young age and otherwise good health appeared to be on her side when subsequent scans showed no evidence of cancer, and doctors declared her clear to go on with life. Jacqueline excitedly began her first semester of a PhD program in sociology.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThen it happened again six years later, when she was 27 years old: Another lump emerged in the same area of her bikini line. Jacqueline visited the gynecologist at her university&#x2019;s health center, who said it was just an inflamed lymph node. &#x201C;If it doesn&#x2019;t bother you, don&#x2019;t bother it,&#x201D; advised the physician. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThis time, Jacqueline wasted no time in seeking a second opinion. A needle biopsy confirmed the dreaded: Stage III melanoma had returned. &#x201C;Even though it was my second diagnosis, I was shocked all over again. My doctor told me, &#x2018;It will be a miracle if you survive another five years,&#x2019;&#x201D; shares Jacqueline.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThe hidden skin cancer risks for people of color&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPerhaps even more surprising is that Jacqueline&#x2019;s case isn&#x2019;t an anomaly. While Caucasians are more likely to be diagnosed with skin cancer, only 16 percent of cases involve advanced-stage cancer. In comparison, 52 percent of African-Americans and 26 percent of Hispanic patients are diagnosed with late-stage cases, according to the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.skincancer.org\u002Fprevention\u002Fskin-cancer-and-skin-of-color\"\u003ESkin Cancer Foundation\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe initial site of Jacqueline&#x2019;s melanoma has never been determined. People of color are more likely to be diagnosed with melanoma in unusual areas like between the toes, under the nails, behind the ears, on the palms of hands and soles of feet, inside the lips, and between the buttock cheeks. Melanoma can even develop in the eyes, the lungs, the gastrointestinal tract, and the membrane known as the meninges that covers the brain and spinal cord.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002F3-tips-to-apply-sunscreen-the-right-way-you-know-119381099947.html\"\u003E3 Tips to Apply Sunscreen the Right Way\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;While we know UV light plays a role in melanomas found on Caucasian skin, the primary risk factors for melanoma in people with skin of color has yet to be determined,&#x201D; New York dermatologist \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.drwhitneybowe.com\"\u003EWhitney Bowe, MD\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, tells Yahoo Health. &#x201C;That&#x2019;s why patients with darker skin may get melanomas in areas that we don&#x2019;t commonly associate with sun exposure.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThis time around for Jacqueline, driving the cancer back into remission was grueling. She had all of her pelvic lymph nodes removed and underwent Interferon drug treatment and radiation over the course of a year that had her coping with painful open wound burns. While she finally did achieve remission, Jacqueline was left with lymphedema in one leg, a permanent severe swelling that is caused by lymphatic system blockage.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I keep the lymphedema in perspective &#x2014; I have two legs that still work and I have my health, yet it&#x2019;s difficult being young and having so many restrictions. Once upon a time, just being able to choose my shoes was something I took for granted &#x2014; now, I can&#x2019;t fit into most regular shoes,&#x201D; she explains.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELymphedema, which Jacqueline cites as her greatest survivor challenge, is a risk associated with lymph node removal after melanoma and breast cancer surgeries. &#x201C;The risk of developing lymphedema is dependent upon the number of lymph nodes removed &#x2014; so if melanoma is diagnosed early, there may be no lymph node dissection at all, and therefore no risk of lymphedema,&#x201D; says Deborah Lindquist, MD, an oncologist with Arizona Oncology, a practice in \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.usoncology.com\"\u003Ethe US Oncology Network\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Lindquist adds that a drug to treat the chronic condition is currently in clinical trials and may be available to the public in the near future.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAccording to the Skin Cancer Foundation, Hispanics account for the highest amount of new skin cancer cases among people of color. &#x201C;Melanoma incidence is increasing rapidly in Latinos, who are outpacing African-Americans likely due to more tanning bed usage,&#x201D; explains New Jersey dermatologist \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fimagedermatology.com\"\u003EJeanine B. Downie\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, MD. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EExperts recommend wearing sunscreen with an SPF of 30 or higher as the best way to prevent skin cancer and melanoma in people of any color. Jacqueline now follows the advice religiously; she always has sunscreen in her bag (favorites include sprays by \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.neutrogena.com\u002Fcategory\u002Fsun\u002Fsunscreen+spray.do\"\u003ENeutrogena\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;such as CoolDry Sport Sunscreen Spray and Ultra Sheer Body Mist Sunscreen), as she finds the spray formulas absorb without the chalkiness of other more traditional formulas. &#x201C;Please don&#x2019;t think you don&#x2019;t need sunscreen because your skin color is natural protectant from the sun &#x2014; anyone with skin is at risk for developing melanoma,&#x201D; she warns. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fthe-scary-causes-behind-the-rise-in-skin-cancer-118288125190.html\"\u003EThe Scary Causes Behind the Rise in Skin Cancer Rates\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EMost importantly, experts say to get familiar with your skin, so that you notice any changes to new or existing spots and moles. Melanoma is virtually always curable if detected early. &#x201C;If the mole is multicolored, very dark, growing rapidly in size, painful, or stands out as totally different from your other moles, have a dermatologist check it out,&#x201D; Downie says. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHave an annual skin checkup with your dermatologist to assess new and old spots, and if you&#x2019;ve previously had precancerous or cancerous lesions, you should go even more regularly &#x2014; every six months. When visiting other doctors like your ophthalmologist and gynecologist, have them check for any unusual signs that you can&#x2019;t see, and ask the same of your hair stylist, who experts say is often your first line of defense against skin cancer on the scalp. &#xA0; &#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn fact, New York hair stylist Roman Kusayev of the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fromanksalon.com\"\u003ERoman K Salon\u003C\u002Fa\u003E recently detected a melanoma on a regular Latina client&#x2019;s scalp while applying hair color. &#x201C;I noticed a suspicious slightly red spot on her scalp that clearly wasn&#x2019;t a wound or scab. I didn&#x2019;t want to scare her, but I knew I had the responsibility to bring it to her attention,&#x201D; Kusayev tells Yahoo Health. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe client soon made an appointment with her dermatologist, who diagnosed the lesion as skin cancer. Fortunately, the early detection made for routine removal. Hairstyles like tightly parted ponytails and tight braids can leave the scalp vulnerable to the sun&#x2019;s UV rays. Experts recommend wearing a hat or brushing hair back when out in the sun so as not to harshly part and expose swaths of scalp to UV rays. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIf you do see something pop up that gives you a funny feeling, Jacqueline says to always trust your instinct. &#x201C;It&#x2019;s important to be your own health advocate. I didn&#x2019;t stop harassing doctors until I definitively found out what was wrong, and that is what saved my life.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ERead This Next: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fthe-part-of-your-face-you-absolutely-need-to-122973275813.html\"\u003EThe Part of Your Face You Absolutely Need to Protect From the Sun \u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ELet&#x2019;s keep in touch! Best Part of Having An Average Face","summary":"According to new research published in Psychological Science, having a typical face has its benefits.","body":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"The Best Part of Having An &#x2018;Average&#x2019; Face\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F8f3aa31506fc8a60cc97a611eb9cb3646f781cd7.jpg\" width=\"500\" height=\"623\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EThe average face of female residents of Sydney, Australia, depicted by the artist Mike Mike.\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E (Image created by Mike Mike | \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ffaceoftomorrow.org\u002F\"\u003EFaceoftomorrow.org\u003C\u002Fa\u003E)\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWhile it&#x2019;s human nature to marvel at a beautiful face, science says we may not exactly view the characteristics of pretty people in the most glowing light.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAccording to \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fpss.sagepub.com\u002Fcontent\u002Fearly\u002F2014\u002F12\u002F11\u002F0956797614554955.abstract\"\u003Enew research\u003C\u002Fa\u003E published in the journal&#xA0;\u003Cem\u003EPsychological Science\u003C\u002Fem\u003E, having a &#x201C;typical&#x201D; face has its benefits, as people seem to consider the faces of Average Joes and Plain Janes the most trustworthy.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ETo conduct the study, researchers digitally combined the faces of 92 different women to get a sum of parts: a &#x201C;typical&#x201D; face. They also conjured up an &#x201C;attractive&#x201D; face by averaging the faces of the 12 most attractive women in another set of photos.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"image\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"500\" height=\"132\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F042c099c12f9aca78fd7acc64c69f58a372cf767.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EThe typical face was found to be more trustworthy than those on the opposite sides of the spectrum.\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E (Carmel Sofer&#xA0;|&#xA0;Psychological Science)\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAfter creating these digital images, they joined the &#x201C;typical&#x201D; face and &#x201C;attractive&#x201D; face into one, and then created nine more images varying in levels of attractiveness and typicality. The final outcome? A total of 11 faces, which were laid out along a spectrum from least attractive to most attractive, with the &#x201C;typical&#x201D; face smack dab in the middle.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ETo nix gender bias, the researchers had only women rate the faces on a 9-point scale for trustworthiness or attractiveness. Over the course of the study, they wound up rating each separate face a total of three times.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"image\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"500\" height=\"534\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F2412a75d6db7f4b6324ed93b6290d40f3e57b45c.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EThe average face lies at the intersection of trustworthiness and attractiveness.\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E (Carmel Sofer&#xA0;|&#xA0;Psychological Science)\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe scientists found that the results revealed something of a &#x201C;U-shape&#x201D; correlation between trustworthiness and attractiveness; the closer an image was to the &#x201C;typical&#x201D; face in the middle of the spectrum, the more trustworthy the women rated it. Attractiveness, on the other hand, had nothing to do with typicality. As expected, moving beyond the central image and up the spectrum, the participants rated each face as more and more attractive.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ESo, why would we trust someone with a &#x201C;typical&#x201D; face? It&#x2019;s simple: generally, we&#x2019;re comfortable with what we know and recognize, while we fear the unknown.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Face typicality likely indicates familiarity and cultural affiliation &#x2014; as such, these findings have important implications for understanding social perception, including cross-cultural perceptions and interactions,&#x201D; says lead researcher Carmel Sofer, a psychological scientist at Princeton University and Radboud University Nijmegen in the Netherlands, in a \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.psychologicalscience.org\u002Findex.php\u002Fnews\u002Freleases\u002Fpeople-trust-typical-looking-faces-most.html\"\u003Epress release\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWith all the science on the potential benefits of being beautiful &#x2014; \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fpress.princeton.edu\u002Ftitles\u002F9516.html\"\u003Ehigher pay\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fpsych.colorado.edu\u002F~tito\u002Fsp03\u002F7536\u002FRhodes_et_al_2001.pdf\"\u003Ebetter health\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, the list goes on &#x2014; at least we know beautiful people don&#x2019;t have it \u003Cem\u003Eall\u003C\u002Fem\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EYour Next Read: \u003Ca
